class="mw-redirect" title="Hindi language">Hindi</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Budget</th><td>\n<span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">\xe2\x82\xb9</a></span>40&#160;million<sup id="cite_ref-Boi2016_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boi2016-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;">Box office</th><td>\n<abbr title="estimation">est.</abbr> <span style="white-space: nowrap">\xe2\x82\xb9</span>1.03&#160;billion<sup id="cite_ref-Boi2016_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boi2016-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table> \n<p><i><b>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</b></i> (English: <i lang="en">The Big-Hearted Will Take Away the Bride</i>), also known by the <a href="/wiki/Initialism" class="mw-redirect" title="Initialism">initialism</a> <i><b>DDLJ</b></i>, is an Indian <a href="/wiki/Romance_film" title="Romance film">romance film</a>, directed by <a href="/wiki/Aditya_Chopra" title="Aditya Chopra">Aditya Chopra</a> (in his directorial debut), produced by his father <a href="/wiki/Yash_Chopra" title="Yash Chopra">Yash Chopra</a>, and written by <a href="/wiki/Javed_Siddiqui" title="Javed Siddiqui">Javed Siddiqui</a> with Aditya Chopra. Released on 20 October <a href="/wiki/Bollywood_films_of_1995" class="mw-redirect" title="Bollywood films of 1995">1995</a>, the film stars <a href="/wiki/Shah_Rukh_Khan" title="Shah Rukh Khan">Shah Rukh Khan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kajol" title="Kajol">Kajol</a>. The plot revolves around Raj and Simran, two young <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">non-resident Indians</a>, who fall in love during a vacation through Europe with their friends. Raj tries to win over Simran\'s family so the couple can marry, but Simran\'s father has long since promised her hand to his friend\'s son. The film was shot in India, London and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, from September 1994 to August 1995.\n</p><p>Earning <span style="white-space: nowrap">\xe2\x82\xb9</span>1.06&#160;billion (valued at about US$32,766,000 in 1995)<sup id="cite_ref-exchange_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exchange-6">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> in India and <span style="white-space: nowrap">\xe2\x82\xb9</span>160&#160;million (valued at about US$4,946,000 in 1995)<sup id="cite_ref-exchange_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exchange-6">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> overseas, <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> became the highest grossing <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> film of the year, and one of the most successful Indian films in history. It won 10 <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a>, the most for a single film at that time, and won the <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Popular_Film_Providing_Wholesome_Entertainment" title="National Film Award for Best Popular Film Providing Wholesome Entertainment">National Film Award for Best Popular Film Providing Wholesome Entertainment</a>. Its soundtrack album became one of the most popular of the 1990s.\n</p><p>Many critics praised the film, which connected with different segments of society by simultaneously promoting strong family values and the following of one\'s own heart. Its success led other film makers to target the non-resident Indian audience, which was deemed more lucrative for them. It spawned many imitations of its story and style, and homages to specific scenes. <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> was one of only three Hindi films in the reference book <i><a href="/wiki/1001_Movies_You_Must_See_Before_You_Die" title="1001 Movies You Must See Before You Die">1001 Movies You Must See Before You Die</a></i>, and was placed twelfth on the <a href="/wiki/British_Film_Institute" title="British Film Institute">British Film Institute</a>\'s list of top Indian films of all time. It is the longest-running film in the history of <a href="/wiki/Indian_cinema" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian cinema">Indian cinema</a>. As of 2018, over 20 years after its first release, it is still being shown at the <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Mandir" title="Maratha Mandir">Maratha Mandir</a> theatre in <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Raj Malhotra (<a href="/wiki/Shah_Rukh_Khan" title="Shah Rukh Khan">Shah Rukh Khan</a>) and Simran Singh (<a href="/wiki/Kajol" title="Kajol">Kajol</a>) are non-resident Indians living in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. Simran was raised by her strict and conservative father, Baldev Singh (<a href="/wiki/Amrish_Puri" title="Amrish Puri">Amrish Puri</a>), while Raj\'s father (<a href="/wiki/Anupam_Kher" title="Anupam Kher">Anupam Kher</a>) is very liberal. Simran always dreams of meeting her ideal man; her mother Lajjo (<a href="/wiki/Farida_Jalal" title="Farida Jalal">Farida Jalal</a>) warns her against this, saying dreams are good, but one should not blindly believe they come true. One day, Baldev receives a letter from his friend Ajit (<a href="/wiki/Satish_Shah" title="Satish Shah">Satish Shah</a>), who lives in <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_India" title="Punjab, India">Punjab</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. Ajit wants to keep a promise he and Baldev made to each other 20 years ago\xe2\x80\x94to have Simran marry his son Kuljeet (<a href="/wiki/Parmeet_Sethi" title="Parmeet Sethi">Parmeet Sethi</a>). Simran is disappointed as she does not want to marry someone whom she has never met.\n</p><p>One evening, Raj enters Baldev\'s shop after closing time to buy beer. Baldev refuses, but Raj grabs a case of beer, throws money on the counter, and runs away. Baldev, infuriated, calls Raj a disgrace to India. Meanwhile, Raj\'s father agrees to his request to go on a train trip across Europe with his friends, and Simran\'s friends have invited her to go on the same trip. Simran asks her father to let her see the world before her marriage, and he reluctantly agrees.\n</p><p>On the trip, Raj and Simran meet. Raj constantly flirts with Simran, much to her irritation. The two miss their train to <a href="/wiki/Zurich" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurich">Zurich</a> and are separated from their friends, but start to travel together and become friends. Raj falls in love with Simran on the journey, and when they part ways in London, Simran realises she is in love with him as well. At home, Simran tells her mother about the boy she met on her trip; Baldev overhears the conversation and becomes enraged with his daughter. He says the family will move to India the next day. Meanwhile, Raj tells his father about Simran and that she will soon get married. When Raj says he believes Simran loves him too, his father encourages him to go after her.\n</p><p>In India, Baldev is reunited with his relatives and his friend Ajit. A miserable Simran and her younger sister Chutki (<a href="/wiki/Pooja_Ruparel" title="Pooja Ruparel">Pooja Ruparel</a>) take an instant dislike to Simran\'s fianc\xc3\xa9 Kuljeet because of his arrogance. Simran pines for Raj, but her mother tells her to forget him because she knows Baldev will never accept their relationship. The next morning, Raj arrives outside of the house where Simran is staying and the two reunite. She begs him to elope with her, but Raj refuses and says he will only marry her with her father\'s consent. Raj befriends Kuljeet and is quickly accepted by both families. Later, his father arrives in India and also becomes friends with Simran\'s and Kuljeet\'s families. Eventually, Lajjo and Chutki discover that Raj is the boy Simran fell in love with in Europe. Lajjo also tells Raj and Simran to run away, but he still refuses. Baldev recognises Raj from the beer incident, but eventually accepts him. However, after he discovers a photograph of Raj and Simran together in Europe, he slaps and humiliates Raj and tells him to leave.\n</p><p>As Raj and his father wait at the railway station, Kuljeet, who is angry to learn of Raj\'s love for Simran, arrives with his friends and attack them. Eventually Baldev and Ajit arrive and stop the fight, and Raj boards the departing train with his father. Simran then arrives with her mother and sister; she tries to join Raj on the train, but Baldev stops her. Simran begs him to let her go, saying she cannot live without Raj. Baldev, realising nobody loves his daughter more than Raj does, lets her go, and she runs and catches the train as it departs.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Credits adapted from <a href="/wiki/British_Film_Institute" title="British Film Institute">British Film Institute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 35em; -webkit-column-width: 35em; column-width: 35em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Shah_Rukh_Khan" title="Shah Rukh Khan">Shah Rukh Khan</a> as Raj Malhotra</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kajol" title="Kajol">Kajol</a> as Simran Singh</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Amrish_Puri" title="Amrish Puri">Amrish Puri</a> as Baldev Singh Chaudhary, Simran\'s father</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Farida_Jalal" title="Farida Jalal">Farida Jalal</a> as Lajwanti "Lajjo" Singh, Simran\'s mother</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Satish_Shah" title="Satish Shah">Satish Shah</a> as Ajit Singh, Baldev\'s friend in India</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Achala_Sachdev" title="Achala Sachdev">Achala Sachdev</a> as Simran\'s grandmother</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Himani_Shivpuri" title="Himani Shivpuri">Himani Shivpuri</a> as Kammo Kaur, Simran\'s aunt</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pooja_Ruparel" title="Pooja Ruparel">Pooja Ruparel</a> as Rajeshwari "Chutki" Singh, Simran\'s sister</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anupam_Kher" title="Anupam Kher">Anupam Kher</a> as Dharamvir Malhotra, Raj\'s father</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Parmeet_Sethi" title="Parmeet Sethi">Parmeet Sethi</a> as Kuljeet Singh, Ajit\'s son</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mandira_Bedi" title="Mandira Bedi">Mandira Bedi</a> as Preeti Singh, Ajit\'s daughter</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anaita_Shroff_Adajania" title="Anaita Shroff Adajania">Anaita Shroff Adajania</a> as Sheena, Simran\'s friend</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a> and Arjun Sablok as Raj\'s friends</li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_and_scripting">Origin and scripting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Origin and scripting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Aditya_Chopra" title="Aditya Chopra">Aditya Chopra</a> assisted his father, director and producer <a href="/wiki/Yash_Chopra" title="Yash Chopra">Yash Chopra</a>, during the making of <i><a href="/wiki/Chandni" title="Chandni">Chandni</a></i> (1989), <i><a href="/wiki/Lamhe" title="Lamhe">Lamhe</a></i> (1991) and <i><a href="/wiki/Darr" title="Darr">Darr</a></i> (1993).<sup id="cite_ref-adi_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adi-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> During this time, Aditya wrote several of his own scripts, including one he assumed would be his first film, but eventually became his second, <i><a href="/wiki/Mohabbatein" title="Mohabbatein">Mohabbatein</a></i> (2000).<sup id="cite_ref-Shahrukh_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shahrukh-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> For three years, he worked on the story that would become <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> before approaching his father to direct it. Yash did not want to, and tried to persuade Aditya to do it himself.<sup id="cite_ref-filmf_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmf-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> As they were discussing ideas for the script, Aditya conceived the notion that Raj would seek permission for marriage from Simran\'s stern father, rather than eloping with her. He then became excited about the possibility of directing the film himself. After his mother, the playback singer <a href="/wiki/Pamela_Chopra" title="Pamela Chopra">Pamela Chopra</a>, agreed that the idea was sound, he decided to make this his directorial debut.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200231\xe2\x80\x9332_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200231\xe2\x80\x9332-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Aditya wanted to make a wholesome film that people could watch repeatedly. He wanted to diverge from the typical plot line of the time, in which lovers run away when their parents object, and show that if their love was strong enough, the parents would eventually understand.<sup id="cite_ref-filmf_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmf-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 1994, Aditya read the first draft of the script to several members of the <a href="/wiki/Yash_Raj_Films" title="Yash Raj Films">Yash Raj Films</a> production team assigned to work with him, including a cinematographer, an art director and a dialogue writer. They were not impressed, but Aditya held fast to his ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200236_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200236-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He was given total editorial control by his father, the producer, and made the film according to his own tastes and sensibilities.<sup id="cite_ref-ff1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ff1-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Aditya struggled with both the dialogue writer <a href="/wiki/Javed_Siddiqui" title="Javed Siddiqui">Javed Siddiqui</a> and the song lyricist <a href="/wiki/Anand_Bakshi" title="Anand Bakshi">Anand Bakshi</a> to develop words that were "young-sounding".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200239_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200239-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> There were personal clashes over writing credits on the final script. Pamela\'s friend <a href="/wiki/Honey_Irani" title="Honey Irani">Honey Irani</a> believed she deserved a writing credit that she did not receive, and Siddiqui believed Aditya did not deserve partial credit for the dialogue. After <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i>, neither of them ever worked with Yash Raj Films again.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200250\xe2\x80\x9351_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200250\xe2\x80\x9351-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> After approving the script, Yash was consulted about the songs, but mostly left the creative process to his son, and has firmly denied that he was a ghost director on the project.<sup id="cite_ref-ff1_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ff1-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> He did not shoot a single frame, and did not even view some portions of the film until it was nearly completed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200244,47_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200244,47-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casting">Casting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Casting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Aditya originally wanted the film to be about a relationship between an Indian and an American. He wanted <a href="/wiki/Tom_Cruise" title="Tom Cruise">Tom Cruise</a> for the role of Raj but was dissuaded by Yash, who did not want to use a foreign star.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> They decided their characters would be non-resident Indians (NRIs). Aditya approached Shah Rukh Khan to play the role of Raj. Shah Rukh was initially not interested because of the romantic nature of the role, having had success playing villainous roles.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200236_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200236-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Aditya then asked <a href="/wiki/Saif_Ali_Khan" title="Saif Ali Khan">Saif Ali Khan</a> to play the lead role because he was having problems persuading Shah Rukh to do it.<sup id="cite_ref-sair_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sair-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Saif declined for unknown reasons,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> as did <a href="/wiki/Aamir_Khan" title="Aamir Khan">Aamir Khan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> causing Aditya to continue pursuing Shah Rukh.<sup id="cite_ref-sair_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sair-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> Aditya and Shah Rukh had four meetings over several weeks; he finally persuaded Shah Rukh by telling him he could never be a superstar unless he became "every woman\'s dream man, and every mother\'s dream son".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200236_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200236-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Since then, Shah Rukh has expressed his gratitude to Aditya for helping to make him a star with this film.<sup id="cite_ref-Shahrukh_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shahrukh-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Shah Rukh said that fellow actor <a href="/wiki/Salman_Khan" title="Salman Khan">Salman Khan</a> also encouraged him to do the role, saying that he thought the film would be very successful.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Shah Rukh has also noted the similarities in the film\'s script to his own relationship with <a href="/wiki/Gauri_Khan" title="Gauri Khan">Gauri Khan</a> before their marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUberoi1997321_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUberoi1997321-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Kajol was the first choice to play Simran, to which she quickly agreed; she was a good friend of Aditya.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200235_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200235-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> She and Shah Rukh had previously worked together in the successful films <i><a href="/wiki/Baazigar" title="Baazigar">Baazigar</a></i> (1993) and <i><a href="/wiki/Karan_Arjun" title="Karan Arjun">Karan Arjun</a></i> (1995).<sup id="cite_ref-couple_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-couple-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Kajol said her character was very difficult for her to relate to, whereas Shah Rukh said Raj\'s personality was very similar to his own.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Aditya chose the name Raj for the character, and the mandolin that he played, based on his admiration for the actor <a href="/wiki/Raj_Kapoor" title="Raj Kapoor">Raj Kapoor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> After a successful <a href="/wiki/Screen_test" title="Screen test">screen test</a>, Parmeet Sethi was chosen over <a href="/wiki/Armaan_Kohli" title="Armaan Kohli">Armaan Kohli</a> for the role of Kuljeet Singh.<sup id="cite_ref-Bookmyshow_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bookmyshow-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In addition to his assistant director <a href="/wiki/Sameer_Sharma_(director)" title="Sameer Sharma (director)">Sameer Sharma</a>, Aditya asked for two additional assistants, his brother <a href="/wiki/Uday_Chopra" title="Uday Chopra">Uday Chopra</a> and his cousin <a href="/wiki/Karan_Johar" title="Karan Johar">Karan Johar</a>. Johar also played a small role in the film as Raj\'s friend.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200234_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200234-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Sharmishta Roy was the film\'s art director<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200233_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200233-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Manish_Malhotra" title="Manish Malhotra">Manish Malhotra</a> was its costume designer. While Malhotra had many new ideas, Aditya wanted to keep the clothing style simple; he did not want it to distract from the story.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200242\xe2\x80\x9343_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200242\xe2\x80\x9343-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, Malhotra was responsible for the idea of Simran wearing a green dress in the song "Mehndi Laga Ke Rakhna", an unusual colour for a Punjabi bride.<sup id="cite_ref-Bookmyshow_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bookmyshow-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Filming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:B-Montbovon-Eglise-Saint-Grat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A church with a high steeple on a green field" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/B-Montbovon-Eglise-Saint-Grat.jpg/220px-B-Montbovon-Eglise-Saint-Grat.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/B-Montbovon-Eglise-Saint-Grat.jpg/330px-B-Montbovon-Eglise-Saint-Grat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/B-Montbovon-Eglise-Saint-Grat.jpg/440px-B-Montbovon-Eglise-Saint-Grat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:B-Montbovon-Eglise-Saint-Grat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Church of Saint Grat in Montbovon, one of the filming locations in Switzerland</div></div></div>\n<p><i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> was filmed in several 5-, 10- and 20-day schedules between September<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>1994 and August<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>1995.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200240_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200240-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The first sequence filmed was for the song "Ho Gaya Hai Tujhko" with Kajol and Shah Rukh in Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The European journey scenes and songs were mainly filmed in <a href="/wiki/Saanen" title="Saanen">Saanen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montbovon" class="mw-redirect" title="Montbovon">Montbovon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gstaad" title="Gstaad">Gstaad</a>, Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt1_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt1-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yrf1_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yrf1-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Other scenes were shot in England, at locations including <a href="/wiki/Trafalgar_Square" title="Trafalgar Square">Trafalgar Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">King\'s Cross railway station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angel_tube_station" title="Angel tube station">Angel Underground station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDwyer201459_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDwyer201459-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Film\'s cinematographer <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh_(director)" class="mw-redirect" title="Manmohan Singh (director)">Manmohan Singh</a>, a regular collaborator with Chopra, shot the song "Tujhe Dekha To", including the iconic mustard fields scenes with Shah Rukh and Kajol in the mustard fields in <a href="/wiki/Gurgaon" title="Gurgaon">Gurgaon</a> on the outskirts of the <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_Region_(India)" title="National Capital Region (India)">National Capital Region Delhi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bookmyshow_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bookmyshow-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\nThe cast faced difficulties while filming the final scene, which shows Simran running to catch the train on which Raj is travelling. The smoldering heat made it difficult to shoot and each time there was a retake, the train took 20 minutes to return.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Saroj_Khan" title="Saroj Khan">Saroj Khan</a> was the choreographer throughout most of the production, but after several disputes between her and Aditya, she was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Farah_Khan" title="Farah Khan">Farah Khan</a> near the end of the shoot. After the film\'s eventual success, Saroj apologised to Aditya for underestimating him, but she never worked with him again.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200252_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200252-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Farah choreographed the song "Ruk Ja O Dil Deewane",<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200245\xe2\x80\x9346_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200245\xe2\x80\x9346-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> during which Aditya did not tell Kajol that Shah Rukh was going to drop her, as he wanted to capture her genuine reaction.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The film\'s title was suggested by actress <a href="/wiki/Kirron_Kher" title="Kirron Kher">Kirron Kher</a>; it came from the song "Le Jayenge Le Jayenge", in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Chor_Machaye_Shor" title="Chor Machaye Shor">Chor Machaye Shor</a></i> (1974).<sup id="cite_ref-epic_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epic-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The Raj character sings parts of this song during the story, and it recurs at the end. <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> is believed to be the only Bollywood film with a "Title suggested by" credit.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200237_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200237-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The film has since become universally known by the acronym <i>DDLJ</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-skj_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skj-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra20028_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra20028-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Towards the end of the <a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">principal photography</a>, Shah Rukh had to split his time between this film and <i><a href="/wiki/Trimurti_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Trimurti (film)">Trimurti</a></i> (1995), spending half of his day on each film.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200246\xe2\x80\x9348_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200246\xe2\x80\x9348-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In early August<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>1995, when filming on <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> was not yet finished, a release date in October around the time of the <a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">Diwali</a> festival was decided upon. Composers Jatin and Lalit Pandit were given only 10 days to complete the background score, and the first copies were printed on 30 September.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200246\xe2\x80\x9348_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200246\xe2\x80\x9348-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> After filming was complete, Aditya decided to make a Hollywood-style documentary of the film-making process, which had not been done before in India. Karan Johar and Uday were put in charge because they had already been recording some of the process. On 18 October, two days before the film\'s release, the 30-minute special <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge, The Making</i> was broadcast on television by <a href="/wiki/Doordarshan" title="Doordarshan">Doordarshan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bookmyshow_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bookmyshow-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200246\xe2\x80\x9348_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200246\xe2\x80\x9348-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Themes">Themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> repeats the usual conservative agenda of family, courtship and marriage, but it proposes that Indian family values are portable assets that can be upheld regardless of country of residence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUberoi1997305,_333_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUberoi1997305,_333-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> To prove this, Raj, an NRI who was brought up in London, is portrayed as the story\'s "good guy", whereas Kuljeet, raised in India, is portrayed as the villain. This is a reversal of the roles in typical Indian films, which usually portray Indians as being morally superior to Westerners.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGanti200442_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGanti200442-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Here, NRIs are validated as potential model Indian citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMehta20111\xe2\x80\x932_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMehta20111\xe2\x80\x932-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The story aims to capture the struggle between traditional family values and the modern value of individualism.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVirdi2003208_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVirdi2003208-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Although Raj and Simran want to be together regardless of her father\'s plans for her, Raj tries to win over his girlfriend\'s father rather than simply eloping with her. In this and other Indian stories, family values are ultimately considered more important than the romantic plot. Moral values and rules of conduct take precedence over individual desires.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDengel-JanicEckstein200851_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDengel-JanicEckstein200851-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The film implies that "Indianness" can be defined by the importance of family life; whether at home or abroad, it is the Indian family system that is recognised as the social institution that most defines Indian identity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPunathambekar2005160_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPunathambekar2005160-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i>, the purity/sanctity of women is being related to that of the nation. In the scene after Raj and Simran spend the night together, and Simran is concerned that something happened, Raj tells her: "You think I am beyond values, but I am a Hindustani, and I know what a Hindustani girl\'s <i>izzat</i> (honour) is worth. Trust me, nothing happened last night." This speaks to the Indian diaspora and their need to try and sustain their value system,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPunathambekar2005158_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPunathambekar2005158-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and the man\'s responsibility to protect the Indian woman\'s sexual purity.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVirdi2003197_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVirdi2003197-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In <i>The Routledge Encyclopedia of Films</i>, Ranjani Mazumdar says the film has a running theme of unfulfilled desires, which is exemplified by Raj\'s father telling him to enjoy life because his own was a struggle, and Simran\'s mother telling her to run away with Raj because she was unable to live her own dreams.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMazumdar2014207_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMazumdar2014207-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scott Jordan Harris, writing for <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a>\'s website, says the film\'s popularity lies in its ability to effectively convey two opposing themes appealing to different portions of society. He said, "It argues that we should follow our hearts and chase happiness wherever it leads, regardless of the obstacles in our paths, while simultaneously suggesting we should respect the ways of our elders, particularly our parents, and do nothing that challenges their will".<sup id="cite_ref-ebert_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ebert-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Rachel Dwyer said the film was important for presenting marriage as an understanding between parents and children. While fighting the old tradition of the arranged marriage, it still encouraged the importance of seeking parental consent, even for a love marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDwyer2014160_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDwyer2014160-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> According to Patricia Uberoi, <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> reiterates the theme of <i><a href="/wiki/Hum_Aapke_Hain_Koun..!" title="Hum Aapke Hain Koun..!">Hum Aapke Hain Koun..!</a></i> (1994)<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> in a self-conscious manner while also linking it explicitly to the fact that the protagonists tend to remind themselves and each other of what it means to be an Indian.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUberoi1997309_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUberoi1997309-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="infobox vevent haudio" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="summary album" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-style: italic; background-color: gainsboro">Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="description" style="text-align:center;background-color: gainsboro"><a href="/wiki/Soundtrack_album" title="Soundtrack album">Soundtrack album</a>&#32;by <span class="contributor"><a href="/wiki/Jatin_Lalit" class="mw-redirect" title="Jatin Lalit">Jatin Lalit</a></span></th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Released</th><td class="published">\n25 July 1995</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">Genre</a></th><td class="category hlist">\n<a href="/wiki/Soundtrack" title="Soundtrack">Feature Film Soundtrack</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Length</th><td>\n<span class="duration"><span class="min">38</span>:<span class="s">46</span></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Record_label" title="Record label">Label</a></th><td class="hlist">\n<a href="/wiki/HMV" title="HMV">HMV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saregama" title="Saregama">Saregama</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">Producer</a></th><td class="hlist">\n<a href="/wiki/Jatin%E2%80%93Lalit" title="Jatin\xe2\x80\x93Lalit">Jatin Lalit</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> soundtrack features seven songs composed by <a href="/wiki/Jatin_Lalit" class="mw-redirect" title="Jatin Lalit">Jatin Lalit</a>, a duo consisting of the brothers Jatin and Lalit Pandit. Anand Bakshi wrote the lyrics and <a href="/wiki/Lata_Mangeshkar" title="Lata Mangeshkar">Lata Mangeshkar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asha_Bhosle" title="Asha Bhosle">Asha Bhosle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kumar_Sanu" title="Kumar Sanu">Kumar Sanu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abhijeet_Bhattacharya" title="Abhijeet Bhattacharya">Abhijeet Bhattacharya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Udit_Narayan" title="Udit Narayan">Udit Narayan</a> performed the vocals.<sup id="cite_ref-itunes_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itunes-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Jatin Lalit was considered for the job when singer Asha Bhosle contacted Yash Chopra after meeting the duo. It was their first collaboration with Yash Raj Films. They secured the job after singing "Mehndi Laga Ke Rakhna" for Yash. In return, they ensured she sang one song, "Zara Sa Jhoom Loon Main". Pamela Chopra helped them select tunes and instruments to give some of the songs a Punjabi flavour.<sup id="cite_ref-rediffmusic_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rediffmusic-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Bhasker Gupta, writing for <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a>, said the soundtrack was the best of Jatin Lalit\'s career, and that it "marked the beginning of the fifth wave in Indian cinema&#160;...".<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The soundtrack became the best-selling <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Bollywood" title="Music of Bollywood">Bollywood soundtrack</a> of the year, with 9\xe2\x80\x9312&#160;million units sold according to <a href="/wiki/HMV" title="HMV">HMV</a>, although it is estimated the same number or more copies were pirated.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra20029_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra20029-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> More than 1&#160;million of those sales occurred prior to the film\'s release.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200246\xe2\x80\x9348_49-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200246\xe2\x80\x9348-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, the album was judged the top Hindi soundtrack of all time by voters on the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Asian_Network" title="BBC Asian Network">BBC Asian Network</a> website.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Anand Bakshi won his third Filmfare Best Lyricist award after 14 years,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERamchandani2003527_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERamchandani2003527-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> having two nominations for this film.<sup id="cite_ref-FFAwardsPDF_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFAwardsPDF-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The wedding song "Mehndi Laga Ke Rakhna" from the film became an all-time hit; it is played at weddings across the South Asian diaspora.<sup id="cite_ref-rediffmusic_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rediffmusic-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mehndi2_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mehndi2-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The following is the track listing.<sup id="cite_ref-itunes_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itunes-63">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="tracklist" style="display:block;border-spacing:0px;border-collapse:collapse;padding:4px"><tbody><tr><th class="tlheader" Mangeshkar">Lata Mangeshkar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Udit_Narayan" title="Udit Narayan">Udit Narayan</a></td><td style="padding-right:10px;text-align:right;vertical-align:top">5:51</td></tr><tr style="background-color:#fff"><td style="padding-right:10px;text-align:right;vertical-align:top">3.</td><td style="vertical-align:top">"Mehndi Laga Ke Rakhna"</td><td style="vertical-align:top">Lata Mangeshkar, Udit Narayan</td><td style="padding-right:10px;text-align:right;vertical-align:top">4:51</td></tr><tr style="background-color:#f7f7f7"><td style="background-color:#f7f7f7"><td style="padding-right:10px;text-align:right;vertical-align:top">6.</td><td style="vertical-align:top">"Tujhe Dekha To"</td><td style="vertical-align:top">Lata Mangeshkar, <a href="/wiki/Kumar_Sanu" title="Kumar Sanu">Kumar Sanu</a></td><td style="padding-right:10px;text-align:right;vertical-align:top">5:05</td></tr><tr style="background-color:#fff"><td style="padding-right:10px;text-align:right;vertical-align:top">7.</td><td style="vertical-align:top">"Zara Sa Jhoom Loon Main"</td><td style="vertical-align:top"><a href="/wiki/Asha_Bhosle" title="Asha Bhosle">Asha Bhosle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abhijeet_Bhattacharya" title="Abhijeet Bhattacharya">Abhijeet Bhattacharya</a></td><td style="padding-right:10px;text-align:right;vertical-align:top">5:55</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> opened on 20 October 1995 to sold-out shows worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-toi800_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toi800-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Every show in every theatre in Mumbai\xe2\x80\x94save one\xe2\x80\x94was completely full for the first week.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200249\xe2\x80\x9350_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200249\xe2\x80\x9350-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The film was popular among both resident Indians and NRIs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESarrazin2008210_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESarrazin2008210-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> At San Francisco\'s 720-seat Naz theatre, 1,000 people arrived for the first showing, and the theatre staff were forced to run another show late that night. In the UK, the film ran for over a year,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200214_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200214-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and as of 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Mandir" title="Maratha Mandir">Maratha Mandir</a> cinema hall in Mumbai has been showing it for more than 22 years.<sup id="cite_ref-thousand_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thousand-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The film earned <span style="white-space: nowrap">\xe2\x82\xb9</span>1.06&#160;billion (valued at about US$32,766,000 in 1995)<sup id="cite_ref-exchange_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exchange-6">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> in India and <span style="white-space: nowrap">\xe2\x82\xb9</span>160&#160;million (valued at about US$4,946,000 in 1995)<sup id="cite_ref-exchange_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exchange-6">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> overseas; it became the biggest Bollywood grosser of the year,<sup id="cite_ref-boi1995_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boi1995-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> and the second highest-grossing film of the 1990s behind <i>Hum Aapke Hain Koun..!</i>. It was the second Bollywood film to gross over <span style="white-space: nowrap">\xe2\x82\xb9</span>1&#160;billion worldwide,<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and one of the biggest Bollywood earners of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-boialltime_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boialltime-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Adjusted for inflation, <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> is among the highest-grossing Hindi films ever;<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> its domestic <a href="/wiki/Net_income" title="Net income">net income</a> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">\xe2\x82\xb9</span>533 million at the time)<sup id="cite_ref-Boi2016_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boi2016-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> is approximately <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">\xe2\x82\xb9</span>4.58 billion</span> (US$64&#160;million) when adjusted for inflation.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> As of 2009, the film had generated over <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">\xe2\x82\xb9</span>60 million</span> (US$840,000) in revenues for the Maratha Mandir since its release.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In later years, that theatre ran one matinee show per day at reduced ticket prices, which averaged about 50% occupancy.<sup id="cite_ref-thousand_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thousand-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> received many favourable reviews.<sup id="cite_ref-toi800_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toi800-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> An initial review by weekly magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Screen_(magazine)" title="Screen (magazine)">Screen</a></i> said of Aditya Chopra, "A young master arrives".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200249\xe2\x80\x9350_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200249\xe2\x80\x9350-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Tom Vick, reviewing the film for <a href="/wiki/Allmovie" class="mw-redirect" title="Allmovie">Allmovie</a>, said, "An immensely likeable movie, <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> performs the rarely achieved feat of stretching a predictable plot over three hours and making every minute enjoyable."<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> When the film toured the US in 2004 as part of the Cinema India showcase, "The Changing Face of Indian Cinema",<sup id="cite_ref-showcase_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-showcase-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Charles Taylor reviewed the film for <i><a href="/wiki/Salon_(website)" title="Salon (website)">Salon</a></i> and said, "It\'s a flawed, contradictory movie\xe2\x80\x94aggressive and tender, stiff and graceful, clich\xc3\xa9d and fresh, sophisticated and naive, traditional and modern. It\'s also, I think, a classic."<sup id="cite_ref-salon_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salon-85">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Writing for <a href="/wiki/NDTV" title="NDTV">NDTV</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anupama_Chopra" title="Anupama Chopra">Anupama Chopra</a> said, "Perhaps the innocence of Raj and Simran\'s romance in which they can spend the night together without sex because Raj, the bratish NRI understands the importance of an Indian woman\'s honor. Perhaps it\'s the way in which the film artfully reaffirms the patriarchal status quo and works for all constituencies\xe2\x80\x94the NRI and the local viewer. Or perhaps it\'s the magic of Shah Rukh Khan and Kajol who created a template for modern love, which was hip and cool but resolutely Indian."<sup id="cite_ref-AC1_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AC1-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> She also called the film a milestone that shaped Hindi cinema through the 1990s, and one of her personal favourites.<sup id="cite_ref-Shahrukh_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shahrukh-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, Meor Shariman of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Malay_Mail" class="mw-redirect" title="The Malay Mail">The Malay Mail</a></i> called the film a "must watch" for Bollywood fans, and also for those seeking an introduction to Bollywood.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Raja_Sen" title="Raja Sen">Raja Sen</a> gave a reflective review for <a href="/wiki/Rediff.com" title="Rediff.com">Rediff.com</a> in 2005, calling the film one of the best Hindi films made in the previous 20&#160;years. He said "Shah Rukh Khan gives a fabulous performance, redefining the Lover for the 1990s with great panache", and called Kajol a "real-as-life actress bringing warmth and credulity" to her role. Sen called the film well balanced and said only the fight scene and some mother-daughter dialogue can wear after multiple viewings.<sup id="cite_ref-Sen_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sen-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Omer M. Mozaffar, writing for <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a>\'s website in 2012, likened the film to a <a href="/wiki/Disney_Princess" title="Disney Princess">Disney Princess</a> story, saying, "the young princess feeling trapped by the traditional patriarchy, seeking freedom through discovering the world, but finally finding it through silent, but inappropriate love. The Little Mermaid. Beauty (of the Beast). Jasmine (friends with Aladdin). Pocahontas. Aurora (Sleeping Beauty). And here, Simran."<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Scott Jordan Harris, also writing for Roger Ebert in 2014, called it "one of the world\'s favorite films", and said it plays as a masterful soap opera, with one of the best screen couples ever seen.<sup id="cite_ref-ebert_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ebert-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sogosurvey" title="Sogosurvey">Sogosurvey</a> conducted an online survey in 2016 in which approximately 47% of the people who participated voted <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> as Bollywood\'s most evergreen love story.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> was ranked among <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times_of_India" title="The Times of India">The Times of India</a>\'</i>s list of the "10 Bollywood movies you must see before you die".<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> It was one of three Hindi films in the film reference book <i><a href="/wiki/1001_Movies_You_Must_See_Before_You_Die" title="1001 Movies You Must See Before You Die">1001 Movies You Must See Before You Die</a></i>, the others being <i><a href="/wiki/Mother_India" title="Mother India">Mother India</a></i> (1957) and <i><a href="/wiki/Deewaar" title="Deewaar">Deewaar</a></i> (1975).<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> It was placed twelfth on the British Film Institute\'s list of top Indian films of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> It is one of the films on Box Office India\'s list of "Biggest Blockbusters Ever in Hindi Cinema".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The film won a <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Awards" title="National Film Awards">National Film Award</a> and 10 <a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Awards" title="Filmfare Awards">Filmfare Awards</a>, setting the record at the time for the most Filmfare trophies.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders sortable">\n<caption>Awards and nominations for <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">Awards\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Category\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Nominee\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Result\n</th>\n<th scope="col" class="unsortable"><abbr title="Reference(s)">Ref(s)</abbr>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/43rd_National_Film_Awards" title="43rd National Film Awards">43rd National Film Awards</a>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/National_Film_Award_for_Best_Popular_Film_Providing_Wholesome_Entertainment" title="National Film Award for Best Popular Film Providing Wholesome rowspan="14" style="text-align:center;"><sup id="cite_ref-FFAwardsPDF_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FFAwardsPDF-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ffwinsshow_99-0" Actress</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Kajol" title="Kajol">Kajol</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Filmfare Award for Best Supporting Award for Best Screenplay">Best Screenplay</a>\n</td>\n<td>Aditya Chopra\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Dialogue" title="Filmfare Award for Best Dialogue">Best Dialogue</a>\n</td>\n<td>Aditya Chopra, <a href="/wiki/Javed_Siddiqui" title="Javed Siddiqui">Javed Siddiqui</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Male_Playback_Singer" title="Filmfare Award for Best Male Playback Singer">Best Male Playback Singer</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Udit_Narayan" title="Udit Narayan">Udit Narayan</a> ("Mehndi Laga Ke Rakhna")\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Filmfare Award for Best Supporting Actor">Best Supporting Actor</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Amrish_Puri" title="Amrish Puri">Amrish Puri</a>\n</td>\n<td rowspan="4" style="background: #FDD; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="no table-no2">Nominated\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Filmfare_Award_for_Best_Music_Director" title="Filmfare Award for Best Music Director">Best Music Director</a>\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Jatin_Lalit" class="mw-redirect" title="Jatin Lalit">Jatin Lalit</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Best Male Playback Singer\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Kumar_Sanu" title="Kumar Sanu">Kumar Sanu</a> ("Tujhe Dekha To")\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Best Lyricist\n</td>\n<td>Anand Bakshi ("Ho Gaya Hai Tujhko To Pyar Sajna")\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row" rowspan="3"><a href="/wiki/Screen_Awards" title="Screen Awards">Screen Awards</a>\n</th>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Star_Screen_Award_for_Best_Film" class="mw-redirect" title="Star Screen Award for Best Film">Best Film</a>\n</td>\n<td>Yash Chopra\n</td>\n<td rowspan="3" style="background: #99FF99; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="yes table-yes2">Won\n</td>\n<td rowspan="3" style="text-align:center;"><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Star_Screen_Award_for_Best_Director" class="mw-redirect" title="Star Screen Award for Best Director">Best Director</a>\n</td>\n<td>Aditya Chopra\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Star_Screen_Award_for_Best_Actor" class="mw-redirect" title="Star Screen Award for Best Actor">Best Actor</a>\n</td>\n<td>Shah Rukh Khan\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historic_box_office_run">Historic box office run</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Historic box office run">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shah_Rukh_Khan_%26_Kajol_unveil_the_special_coffee_table_book_%27DDLJ%27.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Shah Rukh Khan hugs Kajol" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Shah_Rukh_Khan_%26_Kajol_unveil_the_special_coffee_table_book_%27DDLJ%27.jpg/220px-Shah_Rukh_Khan_%26_Kajol_unveil_the_special_coffee_table_book_%27DDLJ%27.jpg" width="220" height="191" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Shah_Rukh_Khan_%26_Kajol_unveil_the_special_coffee_table_book_%27DDLJ%27.jpg/330px-Shah_Rukh_Khan_%26_Kajol_unveil_the_special_coffee_table_book_%27DDLJ%27.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/00/Shah_Rukh_Khan_%26_Kajol_unveil_the_special_coffee_table_book_%27DDLJ%27.jpg 2x" data-file-width="368" data-file-height="320" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shah_Rukh_Khan_%26_Kajol_unveil_the_special_coffee_table_book_%27DDLJ%27.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shah Rukh Khan and Kajol celebrating 1000 weeks of continuous showing of <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> in 2014</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2001, <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> overtook <i><a href="/wiki/Sholay" title="Sholay">Sholay</a></i> (1975), which had run for over five years at the Minerva theatre, as the longest-running film in Indian cinema history.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> It has been showing at the Maratha Mandir theatre (which was famous for having shown <i><a href="/wiki/Mughal-e-Azam" title="Mughal-e-Azam">Mughal-e-Azam</a></i> (1960) for three years) since its original release in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> There are often people in the audience who have seen the film 50 or more times, but still clap, cheer, mouth the dialogues and sing along with the songs,<sup id="cite_ref-Shahrukh_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shahrukh-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra20028_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra20028-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> raising comparisons with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rocky_Horror_Picture_Show" title="The Rocky Horror Picture Show">The Rocky Horror Picture Show</a></i> (1975), the longest running film in America.<sup id="cite_ref-rhps_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rhps-103">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When a theatre strike in early 2011 threatened the film\'s uninterrupted run, the producer Yash Chopra contacted theatre owners to try and ensure the film would continue. He hoped the film would continue to run for at least 1,000 weeks,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> which it achieved in December<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>2014.<sup id="cite_ref-thousand_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thousand-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> To commemorate the event, cast members including Shah Rukh Khan, Kajol, Anupam Kher, Farida Jalal, Mandira Bedi and Pooja Ruparel appeared on the television show <i><a href="/wiki/Comedy_Nights_with_Kapil" title="Comedy Nights with Kapil">Comedy Nights with Kapil</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>  Shah Rukh Khan, Kajol and director Aditya Chopra also attended a live chat with fans and a black tie event at the theatre on 12 December.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The same day, they launched a coffee table book written by Aditya Chopra about the making of the film.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Also in December, Yash Raj Films announced the availability of a collection of commemorative, licensed merchandise from various suppliers to mark the event.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The Maratha Mandir\'s management ended the film\'s run after 1,009 weeks on 19 February<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>2015 because of low attendance (the last show was viewed by 210 people).<sup id="cite_ref-end_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-end-109">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> However, after an outpouring of support from fans, and talks with the production company, they decided to reinstate the film.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence">Influence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Influence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DDLJ_trainscene.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A woman in a dress runs to catch a train while a man is waiting with his hand out to help her" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9b/DDLJ_trainscene.jpg/220px-DDLJ_trainscene.jpg" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9b/DDLJ_trainscene.jpg/330px-DDLJ_trainscene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/9b/DDLJ_trainscene.jpg 2x" data-file-width="412" data-file-height="242" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DDLJ_trainscene.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kajol and Shah Rukh Khan in the climactic train scene</div></div></div>\n<p><i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> spawned many imitators of its story and style, especially throughout the 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChopra200211_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChopra200211-111">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> According to the <i>Encyclopaedia of Hindi Cinema</i>, it and a handful of other films and young directors started a trend for "designer" films. The authors said that these were "a carefully packaged and branded product in which every little visual and physical detail&#160;... is of utmost importance".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChatterjee2003127_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChatterjee2003127-112">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In <i>Bollywood\'s Top 20: Superstars of Indian Cinema</i>, Namrata Joshi said <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> "reinvented Bollywood romances so decisively that we can neatly divide them into two eras\xe2\x80\x94before <i>DDLJ</i> and after <i>DDLJ</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoshi2012235\xe2\x80\x93236_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoshi2012235\xe2\x80\x93236-113">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Yash Raj Films was previously known for using locations outside India for <a href="/wiki/Item_number" title="Item number">item numbers</a> in its films.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPunathambekar2005153_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPunathambekar2005153-114">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> started the trend for films designed to appeal to the Indian diaspora, which have foreign locations as integral parts of the story.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPunathambekar2005153_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPunathambekar2005153-114">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> The characters are themselves diaspora and tend to be able to move with ease between India and the West.<sup id="cite_ref-Hindu1_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hindu1-115">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Some later films that followed this trend include <i><a href="/wiki/Pardes_(film)" title="Pardes (film)">Pardes</a></i> (1997), <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhi_Khushi_Kabhie_Gham..." title="Kabhi Khushi Kabhie Gham...">Kabhi Khushi Kabhie Gham...</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/Kal_Ho_Naa_Ho" title="Kal Ho Naa Ho">Kal Ho Naa Ho</a></i> (2003), <i><a href="/wiki/Salaam_Namaste" title="Salaam Namaste">Salaam Namaste</a></i> (2005), <i><a href="/wiki/Neal_%27n%27_Nikki" title="Neal &#39;n&#39; Nikki">Neal \'n\' Nikki</a></i> (2005) and <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhi_Alvida_Naa_Kehna" title="Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna">Kabhi Alvida Naa Kehna</a></i> (2006).<sup id="cite_ref-Hindu1_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hindu1-115">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMukherjee201245_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMukherjee201245-116">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> became the first Hindi film blockbuster to feature NRIs as main characters.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> It helped to establish the diaspora market as a vital source of revenue for the industry; that market was seen as a safer financial investment than the <a href="/wiki/Desi" title="Desi">desi</a> market.<sup id="cite_ref-Hindu1_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hindu1-115">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several later films have paid homage to <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i>. The Karan Johar-produced <i><a href="/wiki/Humpty_Sharma_Ki_Dulhania" title="Humpty Sharma Ki Dulhania">Humpty Sharma Ki Dulhania</a></i> (2014) was directly inspired by it.<sup id="cite_ref-skj_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skj-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The films <i><a href="/wiki/Jab_We_Met" title="Jab We Met">Jab We Met</a></i> (2007), <i><a href="/wiki/Bodyguard_(2011_Hindi_film)" title="Bodyguard (2011 Hindi film)">Bodyguard</a></i> (2011), <i><a href="/wiki/Chalo_Dilli" title="Chalo Dilli">Chalo Dilli</a></i> (2011), <i><a href="/wiki/Yeh_Jawaani_Hai_Deewani" title="Yeh Jawaani Hai Deewani">Yeh Jawaani Hai Deewani</a></i> (2013) and <i><a href="/wiki/Chennai_Express" title="Chennai Express">Chennai Express</a></i> (2013) include scenes similar to the climactic train sequence, wherein a woman is running to catch a moving train and is helped aboard by a man with his outstretched arm.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The British film <i><a href="/wiki/Slumdog_Millionaire" title="Slumdog Millionaire">Slumdog Millionaire</a></i> (2008) contained a similar train scene, and its final dance sequence was partially shot at the same railway station as the <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i> finale.<sup id="cite_ref-skj_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-skj-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Audiences appreciated the screen chemistry between Shah Rukh Khan and Kajol,<sup id="cite_ref-Sen_88-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sen-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> who later worked together in several successful films including <i><a href="/wiki/Kuch_Kuch_Hota_Hai" title="Kuch Kuch Hota Hai">Kuch Kuch Hota Hai</a></i> (1998), <i><a href="/wiki/Kabhi_Khushi_Kabhie_Gham..." title="Kabhi Khushi Kabhie Gham...">Kabhi Khushi Kabhie Gham...</a></i> (2001), <i><a href="/wiki/My_Name_Is_Khan" title="My Name Is Khan">My Name Is Khan</a></i> (2010), and <i><a href="/wiki/Dilwale_(2015_film)" title="Dilwale (2015 film)">Dilwale</a></i> (2015), and are often referred to as Indian cinema\'s most loved on-screen couple.<sup id="cite_ref-couple_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-couple-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Shah Rukh Khan credits this film with making him a star,<sup id="cite_ref-Shahrukh_9-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shahrukh-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and says it "changed the entire scene for romantic movies of the 90s".<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> During an interview in 2002, he said "Whatever I\'ll stand for as an actor, in the whole of my career, whenever it ends, it will start with and end at <i>Dilwale</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The actress Farida Jalal said the film gave her career a boost, saying she got many offers and "could quote any price".<sup id="cite_ref-quote_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quote-123">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> It also helped the young careers of Pooja Ruparel, who received advertising offers, and of Sharmistha Roy.<sup id="cite_ref-epic_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epic-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The British Film Institute (BFI) commissioned a book about <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i>. It was the first Hindi film chosen for a series of studies on international films, called "BFI Modern Classics". The author was Anupama Chopra and the book was released in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-adi_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adi-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> It was reissued in paperback by Harper-Collins as <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge: The Making of a Blockbuster</i> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> After an unexpectedly long delay, the film was released on DVD by Yash Raj Films in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-uiowa_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uiowa-127">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The release included <i>The Making</i> and <i>300 Weeks Celebration</i> documentaries, <i>Success Story</i> (highlights from the film\'s premiere), clips from the <a href="/wiki/41st_Filmfare_Awards" title="41st Filmfare Awards">41st Filmfare Awards</a> ceremony and other interviews.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, members of the film crew were honoured at a dinner event to celebrate the film\'s 500th week since release. It was hosted by the Consulate General of Switzerland in Mumbai and by Switzerland Tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, Yash Raj Films signed an agreement with Indian and Swiss tour companies to provide a tour package called "YRF Enchanted Journey", to allow visitors to Switzerland to view filming locations used for famous Yash Raj films including <i>Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt1_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt1-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yrf1_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yrf1-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, Yash Raj Films released <i>Aditya Chopra Relives&#160;... Dilwale Dulhania Le Jayenge (As Told to Nasreen Munni Kabir)</i>, an attractive but expensive book about the making of the film.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In response to Indian prime minister <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a> quoting the line "May the force be with you" from the American film franchise <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> during a visit to the US, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> decided to quote a line from a Hindi film during his visit to India in January<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>2015. He chose a line from this film, "<i>Senorita, bade bade deshon mein&#160;...</i>" (Miss, in large countries&#160;...), and added "you know what I mean".<sup id="cite_ref-hindustantimes-obama_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hindustantimes-obama-131">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dilwale_Dulhania_Le_Jayenge&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-exchange-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-exchange_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-exchange_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-exchange_6-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-exchange_6-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The exchange rate in 1995 was 32.35 Indian rupees (<span style="white-space: nowrap">\xe2\x82\xb9</span>) per 1 US dollar (US$).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Other sources claim that Saif was approached for the role before Shah Rukh, so this point is not entirely clear.<sup id="cite_ref-epic_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-epic-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Uberoi states the theme to be that the lovers were willing to sacrifice their own feelings for their families.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEUberoi1997309_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEUberoi1997309-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-97"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-97">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The record has since been tied by <i><a href="/wiki/Devdas_(2002_Hindi_film)" title="Devdas (2002 Hindi film)">Devdas</a></i> (2002), and broken by <i><a href="/wiki/Black_(2005_film)" title="Black (2005 film)">Black</a></i> (2005).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
